text:
This was very good! The basic recipe is excellent, but I made a few tweaks:
I crumbled and saute'd two sweet Italian sausages and mixed with the chicken.
I peeled and cubed 1/2" pieces, two medium red potatoes. Par-cooked them in lightly salted water so they were almost tender. Added them to the vegetables just before adding the flour, which I increased to 1/3 cup plus 2 tablespoons.
I had no broth so I used chicken base and added it to 3 cups water- according to pkg. instructions.
I had no 1/2 and 1/2, so I used a whole can of evaporated milk.
This mixture filled a 9x13" Corning-ware baking dish and I still had room for the biscuits.
I made my own drop biscuits:
Mix together:
2 cups flour
2 tsp. baking powder
1/4 tsp baking soda
1 tsp salt
Cut in:
1/4 shortening
Stir in:
1 cup buttermilk
Drop over chicken mixture as stated and then bake at 400 for the 20-25 minutes.

text:
Wow - a little bit of work, since you have to cook the filling, then bake the potpie, but worth it. I made the recipe as listed with a few minor variations - I added a few turnips to the vegetable mix, because I had them in the fridge. I used fat-free half-and-half and skipped the egg yolk wash on the biscuits. The filling had a great flavor, with the thyme, and the sauce was the perfect consistency, not too thick but not too thin. I used regular Pillsbury Grands refrigerated biscuits (in the can) and they made a great topping. I only used about five in a circle around the top, so there was a little space in between, which I think helps them brown and cook through more (because steam can escape the filling mixture as it heats). A homey, filling meal.

text:
My family LOVED this. I've made it twice, and I've only changed two small things. The first is that both times I've used less half and half than is called for (about half, and the other half 1% milk). Also, the first time I made this I didn't like how doughy the biscuits were on the bottom, so the second time I actually arranged them on a cookie sheet (so they were touching like they would on the pot pie) and baked them separately from the pot pie for about 6 - 7 minutes before putting them top of the filling and continuing to bake the whole thing.

text:
This recipe was great!  I also added a little corn that I cut off of a leftover corn on the cob, and a diced med red potato (just because I wanted to use them up).  I didn't have half and half on hand, so I used whole milk.  I had made an oven roasted chicken with veggies the night before and used the leftover chicken for this.  I also threw in the leftover veggies.    I didn have any refrigerated biscuits, so I used this recipe that I found on this site:
  1 cup all-purpose flour
1 1/2 teaspoons baking powder
1/8 teaspoon salt
1/2 cup milk
1 teaspoon butter or margarine, melted
One of the reviewers for this recipe warned to only mix this until just blended or they would be tough.
I doubled the recipe, divided it into 8 biscuits, and just dropped them onto the mixture.  Baked all in the oven at 350 for 25-30 min.

text:
We loved this recipe.  In addition I located a great recipe on how to pre-cook the chicken so that it did not get dry or chewy:
I used breast tenders.  If they are not equal thickness you can use a meat tenderizer tool to fix that. Mix 1/4 cup of flour and add either dry or finely diced herbs of your choice.  I used a little rosemary, thyme and sage.  Pre-heat a skillet, add approx 2 tbl of butter and 4 tbl of olive oil.  Salt and pepper each piece of chicken and then quickly touch each side in the flour (more like a thin dusting) and place into the hot skillet of butter and oil.  Cook for 1 minute on medium, flip the pieces over and lower the flame to medium-low and cook for 10 minutes covered.  Do not open the lid!  Turn off the heat and allow to sit for another 10 minutes again without every lifting the lid.  The should be moist and tender and ready to add to your chicken pot pie.

text:
This dish was delicious!  I followed the steps of the recipe exactly.  The only additions I made was 1 small potato (cooked with the carrots/celery) and almost 1 can of corn (added with the peas).  I did use canned peas instead of frozen as that's all I had.  For the chicken I cooked that quickly using Goya Sazonador Total seasoning.  I pre-bake the biscuits per other reviews and they were perfectly done after I baked the whole dish.  I did add a little more half and half & broth because I like a lot of gravy.  I cooked and baked the whole thing, including the chicken, in one pan so clean up was really quick.  While the chicken cooked I pre-baked the biscuits (about 5 minutes) and chopped all the veggies.  Besides the Goya seasoning on the chicken, I didn't add any other spices beyond what's listed in the recipe.  I will absolutely make this again (with even more gravy next time!).  Yum!

text:
Made it t but made many changes and made it my own started on cook top, moved to oven.
2 c cream of celery, 2 carrots cut up, 1-onion, (I love garlic) so cut @ minced full clove, 3 celery stalks, 1-c chicken broth, 1-can chicken, added 1- kielbasa cut slim, 6- small red potatoes, 1-C chicken broth, 1 C milk w/ vinegar to substitute for cream.
I sauted garlic, onion in 1 tsp olive oil, added celery then carrots, broth, cans of cream of celery soup. After seasoning everything with this and that, Italian seasoning (no salt) added red potatoes on cook top (stove) 10 min between saute and boiling all flavors together w/chick & kielbasa.
  (cooked potatoes on micro for 5 min first) then combined in bowl.  Cooked in oven 375/convect  400 reg temp w/o biscuits for 40 min first then removed added rolled out jiffy biscuits, cooked for 10-15 min longer  checked until biscuits were brown all in 9x13 glass pan. Nice recipe idea.  I made it my own with base ingredients, did not need flour at all.

Made exactly as directed, except I cut my biscuits in half since I was short on time and didnt have the time to wait for them to take longer.   I really liked the way the biscuits came out, with the egg yolk on top.  My kids were thrilled to have plain biscuits anyway.  Rotisserie chicken made this fast.   The most time consuming part was cutting the veggies.  I also used a pot that could go from the stove to the oven so clean up was a breeze.   My five stars are based on decent flavor (though Im not a fan of thyme so Ill substitute something else next time),  and ease of the recipe.

I may have written a prior review - not sure. But just to pass the word, this is a great and easy recipe. I've probably made it 6-8 times, following recipe, and it never fails. I use canned biscuits and tear them in half because I don't like lots of the crusty/doughy stuff. As another reviewer suggested, I make it in my iron skillet for a one pot meal. Really good! As for biscuits, I use the Grands, 5 count, tear them in half to make 10 and find of stretch them a bit, and they cover perfectly, puff up, and cook thoroughly. I do watch the salt as the broth can be a bit salty. I just add to taste after cooking.

text:
My family LOVED this! The kids were scooping it out of the skillet with a spoon before I could even get it in the oven. :) I made very few changes. I used a Publix rotisserie mojo chicken, which yields around 3-3 1/2 cups when well-picked. I used 4 carrots, 2 ribs of celery, 1/2 a sweet onion, and I substituted corn for the peas, because my family likes corn better. Like some other reviewers, I used Pillsbury Grands *Junior* size biscuits so they would cook well, and I made extra biscuits on the side. I was tempted to thicken up the sauce with cornstarch, but was glad I didn't. By the time it simmered for a while and I added the chicken, it thickened right up on its own. My family loved this, and I will definitely make it again!
*11/12/15: Made this for the second time tonight and it's still a hit! I used the regular sized Grands biscuits this time and it turned out fine. Cooked the whole thing, from start to finish, in my new pre-seasoned cast iron deep skillet and it turned out fantastic. And only one pot to clean is always a plus ;) This recipe is definitely in my rotation of favorite meals now!

text:
Simple and delicious! You can add any veggies that suit you. I always add a clove of minced garlic and I often add sauteed mushrooms as well. But the key to nicely baked biscuits is to make sure the filling is bubbling hot BEFORE adding the biscuits on top. So either heat it through thoroughly on the stove, then add biscuits and place in oven, or put the filling in the oven until nice and bubbly, then add biscuits and continue baking until they are baked through. Enjoy!!

text:
I had to make a couple of minor changes to use what I had, but followed the recipe closely. I used a 12 oz can of Grands jr biscuits instead of the 16 oz can, and dried parsley instead of fresh ( although I'm sure fresh would have been better).  I kept everything else the same with excellent results.  My husband LOVED it and the kids liked it fine.  The only thing I would do differently is cut the biscuits in quarters before adding...some of the ones in the middle were still on the doughy side underneath even though they were nicely browned on top.  This took awhile to put together but was easy and much better than premade pot pies.  Great comfort food on a chilly day!  Thanks for sharing.

I made this last night and it turned out great.  Instead of fresh vegetables and chopped fresh parsley, I just bought a can of mixed vegetables and parsley seasoning (from our spice rack) and used those.  It sped the process up a lot and still taste great.  

I used a 2 quart baking dish as recommended, however mine was too large and it actually took 2 cans of biscuits to cover the top completely.  Also, because of the size of the dish, the pot pie was a little too thin underneath the biscuits.  If you use a 2 quart dish, I'd recommend one smaller with higher sides.

This is wonderful!  First time making chicken pot pie and didn't have any pie crust on hand so searched for a biscuit top version.  So glad I picked this one!  It was DELICIOUS!  I boiled a package of chicken tenderloins while I sauteed the carrots, celery, and onion, and then just did a rough chop on the chicken. Delicious! Excellent base recipe! My husband said it was incredible. I made mine in the cast iron skillet. Only changes I made were to add a little more peas and add potatoes. I like potatoes in my pot pie. So I cut up about a cup of petite golden potatoes and boiled them until you can pierce with a fork. Then I added them at the same time as the chicken. I used a rotisserie chicken from the grocery store. I also baked the biscuits for 6 minutes by themselves before putting on top of the pie after reading a few comments that said the biscuits did not cook through. So good we will make this often!

text:
I've made this twice now & love it. Of course I slightly modify the recipe each time, that's what I do.  Both times I've used the already premade frozen biscuit, not in can as this recipe calls for and I will continue to do so because I like this type of biscuit better.  Although the 1st time I made I used only 6 biscuits, which cooked thoroughly and evenly around sides of biscuits due to extra spacing between biscuits. However the 2nd time I made I put 8 biscuits which took longer to cook sides of biscuits, due to less spacing, touching each other. They turned out a little gummy, so I  kept cooking until more evenly cooked around the sides. Also more biscuits seemed to take up more moisture/liquid from remainder of dish. To me main part of having biscuit it to enjoy sopping up that gravy. Although both times my genuine pigs (LOL) loved it.  This recipe is a keeper with only 6 frozen premade biscuits. Super easy and less mess than chicken and dumplings.

I have never liked chicken pot pie-the traditional stuff I remember eating as a kid was awful but this recipe looked to delicious to pass up and I was right!

No frozen veggies and a delicious sauce with the biscuits all put a great spin on this classic. (And there's actually a fabulous amount of topping to filling ratio)

Took a little bit more prep time than anticipated but definitely worth it! And despite using a pan and not a cooking dish, the pie actually held together really well and didn't slop everywhere.

Also, I accidentally bought Honey Butter Grands biscuits but would HIGHLY recommend because this blunder made it taste even better

text:
Agree with many other reviewers, this is the best chicken pot pie recipe I've ever found, delicious!  I followed the recipe exactly, but used Pillsbury refrigerated pie crusts instead of canned biscuits.  I used one crust to line the bottom of the pan, pierce bottom and sides, and bake for 8 minutes or until light brown.  Add filling on top of bottom/baked crust, then cover with top crust, pierce to vent, then bake per instructions.  Wonderful!

text:
I took a hint from LALAFLUTIST and prepared and baked this in my cast iron skillet.  Fortunately I had the sense to put a cookie sheet under it because it did overflow.  The recipe  allows a lot of leeway for amounts of vegetables and chicken, and although I didn't add any vegetables not included in the recipe,  if you feel like it, go for it.   If you go by the color of the biscuits, not by the time elapsed, I don't think you will have any problem with underdone biscuits.  Let them get nice and brown.  (I didn't use the egg wash).   Overall it was a satisfying dish.  Not the best chicken pot pie I've ever had, but good enough.

text:
This is a great from scratch recipe which is easily modified with what you have on hand. I increased the vegetables by 2 cups and that required another cup of flour. The sauce came out thick and creamy. If you are using fresh, raw chicken then boil 1/2 a chicken in a large pot with skin on. This will make for fresh chicken broth and you can remove skin, debone and dice into chunks after boiled. I used some fresh herbs from my garden. If you do not have fresh parsley remember when using dried herbs it requires less. I also used 3 biscuits split in half into 6 discs. I place them in bottom of casserole dish and cook til golden before adding the mixture and remaining 6 biscuits on top. This creates a nice bottom crust.

My family loved this recipe. I used frozen chicken tenderloins and a breast (what I had). I boiled them in salted water for a a few minutes, turned down the heat and let them simmer while I prepared the rest of the recipe. When the chicken was done, I shredded it. I also used 2 small tbsp of dried parsley because I didn't have fresh. I didn't have half and half so I substituted 1/3 cup Mexican table cream (thin creme fraishe) and 1/3 cup regular soy milk.  I omitted the celery because I didn't have that either.  I used Pillsbury butter tasting flaky biscuits. It turned out great! Thanks for a great recipe. I will share this one with my sister. We always share recipes that are quick and that the whole family will love.

city:

region:

country:

text:
Tasty; good base recipe.  I prefer to add sauteed mushrooms; I've also added broccoli florets (cauliflower would be good, too).  I have to suggestions, though:  (1) Don't add the peas while cooking the veggies with the flour -- they end up overcooked after being in the oven.  I add them just before the oven stage - cooking them very briefly on the stove first.   (2) I always increase the sauce quantity -- we like enough sauce to clean up with the biscuits!   (3) It's very easy to make your own homemade biscuit dough -- honest!  The Pilsbury dough is so chemical-tasting (and it IS full of nasty ingredients).    (4)  I've actually stopped putting the raw biscuit dough on top of the stew to cook -- I bake them slightly on a baking sheet first, because them always seem to be too doughy on the bottom/middle, but the tops will burn if cooked long enough to mitigate that.  Yes, the oven temp could be lowered, of course, but that just takes too long!  The biscuits can be baking for a few minutes while you're fiinishing up with the stew on the stove.    One more caution: if you decide to use rotisserie chicken, remember that it is always loaded with salt...

text:
This is very tasty and easy.  I used the store roasted chicken as suggested for ease. I also sliced the biscuits in half and used them on the bottom and top (12 biscuits total).  This actually made serving easy since I used a 13x9 Pyrex and there were 12 individual portions. I did saute the onions and celery but added 2 cloves of garlic and used 1 bag of Birdseye Steamfresh mixed vegetables instead of carrots and peas since I wanted corn in the pie.  Finally to cut on fat, I substituted plain Greek nonfat yogurt (2 small individual serving containers, 5.3 oz each) for half and half.  Everyone liked, my husband had a few helpings, and my most picky 8-year old daughter ate it all!

text:
I made this this weekend and it was really good.  With the ingredients listed by # of items insead of cup measures, it's hard to be precise with measurements.  I think my "3 celery ribs" must have been larger than the average, because mine was very celery heavy.  Other than that, the filling was very creamy, homey, and tasty.  I did add a few shakes of poultry seasoning when I tasted it before adding the biscuits to give it a little oommph.  Also, I made a quick homemade stock with the rotisserie chicken parts after I picked the chicken for the meat and used that in place of chicken broth.  Oh, and I skipped the egg wash (lazy).  My biggest issue with this recipe should have been obvious before I started.  I made the full recipe for my 4 person family and we had about 1/2 the dish left over.  The biscuits would have disintegrated if I put it away all together.  I had to remove the biscuits, scrape off the sauce, throw them in the cooling oven upside-down for a bit to dry up, and store them separately so the leftovers would be edible.  How dumb am I?  Next time I will either make a half batch for my light eating family OR just make the biscuits separately and pour the filling over "a la king" style.  Oh, and I like some potatoes in my pot pie, so I'll probably add just a couple small cooked potatoes next time.

Delicious! I followed the directions to a "t." The only suggestion by my husband was to double the chicken filling as, in his opinion, the ratio between biscuit and filling was a little heavy on the biscuit. I used a rotisserie chicken and just pulled the meat off and tore it into chunks. The method for adding the flour to the vegetables first and then the broth and half/half was new to me. It made a perfect lump-free gravy. I'll make this again very soon.
